# 🏫 School of AI — OpenClaw Conversational AI System Playbook — v6.0

> ## 🤖 AI-FACING: TEACH YOURSELF PROTOCOL — READ THIS FIRST
> **You are the agent that will build this system.** Before executing anything below:
> 1. **Orient via Self-Orientation Phase 0 (Steps O.1–O.7).** Apply the **Teach Yourself
>    Protocol** (Step O.1) FIRST — discover the master-files folder, verify the installed
>    OpenClaw version against `docs.openclaw.ai`, run the Backup Protocol, locate the
>    secrets env file. Do not skip orientation to "save time."
> 2. **Route knowledge to the right home — keep the bootstrap layer LEAN.** The core md
>    files (`AGENTS.md`, `TOOLS.md`, `MEMORY.md`, `IDENTITY.md`, `SOUL.md`, `USER.md`) get
>    **only concise pointers** — a 1–2 line note plus the master-files path. Full protocols,
>    full playbooks, full standards, examples, and JSON blocks live in the **master-files
>    folder**, NOT inlined into core md files. Inlining bloat into AGENTS.md/TOOLS.md is the
>    #1 way to degrade the running agent. When this playbook says "the agent reads X on every
>    turn," that means a registry/pointer read — never a wall of pasted text.
> 3. **The GHL hook structure is settled.** Inbound GHL webhooks use a **23-key FLAT** Raw
>    Body, the server `hooks.mappings` entry holds the templated `messageTemplate`, the body's
>    own `messageTemplate` value is **placeholder-free**, `deliver` is **`false`**, and
>    `fallbacks` is **never** a mapping key. If you ever find a passage that disagrees, the
>    **CORRECTED GHL HOOK STRUCTURE (2026-05-29)** section of `GHL-INBOUND-AND-PLAYBOOKS.md`
>    wins — and you should treat the disagreeing passage as a bug to report, not a choice.

> ## 👋 HUMAN / CLASS INTRO (for the School of AI cohort)
> This is the complete, classroom-grade walkthrough of how we stand up a real
> conversational-AI system for a client: an OpenClaw agent that listens on eight channels
> (SMS, Email, Facebook Messenger, Facebook Comments, Instagram, LinkedIn, Live Chat,
> All-in-One Chat), filters spam, remembers each contact's history, replies in the brand's
> voice through GoHighLevel / Convert and Flow, and takes real business actions (booking,
> invoicing, escalating to a human). It is long on purpose — it is the full system, not a
> summary. Read the **AI-FACING** box above if you are the building agent; read the section
> headers and the **Execution Order Map** below if you are a human following along in class.
> Every step is sequenced, gated, and verifiable. Nothing here is improvised.

# OpenClaw Conversational AI System — Complete AI-Facing Setup Playbook

**Purpose:** An end-to-end playbook the client's AI uses to stand up a complete conversational AI system on OpenClaw. The agent receives webhooks from eight channels (SMS, Email, Facebook Messenger, Facebook Comments, Instagram, LinkedIn, Live Chat, All-in-One Chat), classifies inbound messages to filter spam/marketing, reads per-contact conversation history for continuity, replies via the installed GHL skill, and takes business actions (book appointments, send invoices, escalate to humans). The system's primary purpose is conversational AI but the architecture is general — any external API (Stripe, n8n, Calendly, custom CRMs) plugs in the same way via additional `hooks.mappings` entries.

**Portability:** All playbooks, protocols, and configuration documents are written in platform-neutral language. If a client migrates from OpenClaw to another conversational AI platform (Hermes, etc.), the instruction documents travel with them. Only the underlying tunnel + gateway plumbing changes.

**Target version:** OpenClaw 2026.4+ (verified against `docs.openclaw.ai` — with self-verification, agent MUST check the live OpenClaw docs against the actual installed version before applying any config edits, per Self-Orientation Step O.3)
**Version:** 6.0
**Last updated:** May 29, 2026

**What's new in v6.0:** Consolidation + conflict-elimination release. (1) Every GHL hook
passage reconciled to the single **23-key FLAT body** standard — no nested bodies, no
`deliver:true`, no mapping-level `fallbacks`, in-body `messageTemplate` kept placeholder-free,
server-mapping `sessionKey` is `"{{session_key}}"`. Any older contradicting guidance was
removed or corrected; where this playbook and `GHL-INBOUND-AND-PLAYBOOKS.md` disagreed, that
doc wins. (2) The **Communications Playbook Standard** and the **Workflow-AI Instructions
Standard** are integrated in-line as the authoritative single copy (THE TRINITY: every
communications playbook implies a matching workflow-AI prompt and a GHL workflow). (3) Stale
version-history claims corrected (the v4.0 "arbitrary nested payloads" / nested session-key
line and the v4.4 "model+fallbacks into hooks.mappings" line were both wrong and are now fixed
to match the 23-key flat / no-mapping-fallbacks standard). (4) Top-of-file AI-FACING Teach
Yourself callout + human/class intro added. (5) v6.0 title/banner. No real system coverage was
removed — only stale or duplicated text.

**What's new in v5.14:** Two features shipped together — closing out the System Health & Tuning cluster (F35 shipped in v5.12, now F36 + F37 complete it). (1) **Step 9.35 — Monthly Comprehensive Playbook Review.** Runs 1st of each month at 9am via existing `system-health-heartbeat` cron. Deep audit across six dimensions: all Conversation Playbooks (performance, outdated references, scope overlap, retirement candidates), all GHL workflows (firing volume, webhook health, split candidates per Rule 1), Typed Knowledge Bases (last updated, hit rate, stale sources, Dreaming consolidation pace), model configurations (latency trends, fallback hit rates, cost trends), accumulated weekly tune-ups (acceptance follow-through, deferred items ready for action, ignored-but-recurring patterns), bug log (recurring failures, new error types). Outputs prescriptive report with major recommendations (operator decisions) and minor improvements (agent can apply with approval). Reports saved to `<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/tune-ups/YYYY-MM-comprehensive.md`. Operator approves YES/DEFER/IGNORE per item. Recommended model: highest-reasoning available. Manual trigger: "Run a monthly review now". (2) **Step 9.36 — Model Version Freshness Checker.** Weekly check bundled into existing Saturday 11pm proactive-suggestions-scan cron (one consolidated weekend report instead of two). Checks Ollama Cloud catalog, Ollama local manifests (`ollama pull --dry-run`), OpenRouter catalog, direct provider APIs (Anthropic, Google, OpenAI, DeepSeek), embedding model freshness. Categorizes updates: MAJOR (Kimi 2.x → 3.x, DeepSeek V4 → V5 — review release notes carefully), MINOR (incremental — likely safe), PATCH (bug fixes only — usually safe). Operator approves YES (update + post-update synthetic test + auto-rollback if test fails) / NO (dismiss) / DEFER (ask next week). NEVER auto-updates primary models. Embedding updates require full re-index BEFORE switching over. Config backups to `<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/model-config-backups/` before every update. MEMORY.md Rule 14 added. Allow-list action 17 (model config updates) noted as pending refresh.

**What's new in v5.13:** Steps 9.33 + 9.34 (Intelligent Playbook Routing + Proactive Features Suite).

**What's new in v5.3:** Massive feature build. Five Round-2 features promoted to implemented (multi-channel notifications, analytics dashboard, document generation, smart booking, conversation workflow builder). Self-Orientation Step O.6 (Dreaming + Embeddings). Teach Yourself Protocol hardened with per-file routing rules.

**What's new in v5.2:** Step 9.15 prompt injection protection (allow-list architecture, runs FIRST). Subagent enhancements — 10-min heartbeat with 90-min hard cap, explicit choice at start, context window check with `/new` recommendation.

**What's new in v5.1:** Step 9.13 conversational drift detection, Step 9.14 Knowledge Sources system, subagent execution pattern default.

**What's new in v5.0:** All 10 features from original strategic roadmap implemented. Execution discipline hardened with Rules of Engagement, Execution Order Map, mid-run QC checkpoints, Run Manifest.

---

## 🏷️ Terminology

This system has a few distinct components with distinct names. Getting them right matters:

- **Convert and Flow** = Christy's white-label version of GoHighLevel. It IS GHL, with Convert and Flow branding on top. Client-facing materials should refer to "Convert and Flow" rather than "GoHighLevel" when speaking to her clients. Functionally it's identical to GHL — same API endpoints (`services.leadconnectorhq.com`), same workflow builder, same Conversations system. The brand differs; the technology doesn't.

- **OpenClaw** = the AI agent platform that runs the conversational AI. Receives webhooks from Convert and Flow, processes them, replies via the installed GHL skill, takes actions like booking and invoicing.

- **The Conversational AI System** = the complete deployed setup. This is what this playbook builds — OpenClaw + Convert and Flow + the playbooks, protocols, and capabilities documents created during setup. There's no consumer-facing brand name for this whole stack; it's just "the conversational AI system" or "Christy's AI" when talking to a client.

When the agent is writing client-facing artifacts (Client Reference Sheet, communication playbooks, the overview PDF), it uses **Convert and Flow** to refer to the CRM layer. When writing AI-facing technical instructions (curl commands, API endpoints, JSON schemas), it uses **GHL** or **GoHighLevel** because those are the literal technical names at the API layer. Both refer to the same product — just different audiences.

---

## ⚖️ RULES OF ENGAGEMENT (READ THIS BEFORE TOUCHING ANYTHING)

These rules govern how the agent executes this playbook. They are not suggestions.

**Rule 1 — Follow the playbook to the letter.** Every step has been carefully designed, sequenced, and validated. The agent does not improvise, does not add steps "to be helpful," does not skip steps that seem redundant, and does not reorder steps for efficiency. Execute in the exact order specified.

**Rule 2 — Two and only two reasons to deviate.** The agent has explicit permission to adapt the playbook in exactly these cases, and only these cases:

  (a) **Documented OpenClaw schema change.** The agent has verified at `docs.openclaw.ai` and the OpenClaw GitHub `configuration-reference.md` that a field name, required parameter, or endpoint pattern has changed since this playbook was written. The agent must cite the doc URL and the specific change before adapting. Inference is not proof — only literal contradiction between the playbook and the current docs justifies a deviation.

  (b) **Unmet precondition on the client's machine.** A step's prerequisite isn't satisfied (e.g., the expected file doesn't exist, a command returns an unexpected error, an API key is missing). The agent stops, reports the unmet precondition to the operator, and waits for guidance before adapting.

**Rule 3 — No silent deviations.** Every deviation, however small, is logged to the Run Manifest with the reason, the doc evidence (if Rule 2a), and what was done instead. Future agents reading the manifest can audit what happened.

**Rule 4 — Stop at hard failures.** If a step fails irrecoverably (Cloudflare API returns 403 with no recovery path, OpenClaw config validation rejects the new block, the tunnel doesn't connect after 3 retries), the agent STOPS, restores any backups taken, reports the failure, and waits. The agent does NOT keep going hoping the next step compensates.

**Rule 5 — Verify before acting on irreversible changes.** Before any operation that's hard to undo (DNS record creation, cron job registration, config file writes), the agent does a dry-run check OR confirms with the operator. Backups must exist before any config edit.

**Rule 6 — The QC checkpoints are gates, not suggestions.** Mid-execution QC checkpoints (after each phase) must pass before moving to the next phase. A failed checkpoint means stop, report, and wait for operator decision.

**Rule 7 — One value per key. Proper JSON structure, always.** Never cram multiple distinct values into a single string field. Each distinct value gets its own key — nested or flat as the schema requires. This applies to every config edit, every hook payload, every secrets-env line, and every reusable-values record. Concretely: do NOT pack `{ "tunnel": "id=abc; token=eyJ...; host=client.example.com" }` into one string — write `{ "tunnel_id": "abc", "connector_token": "eyJ...", "public_hostname": "client.example.com" }` instead. Combined-string fields silently break downstream parsers and make the reusable-values record un-readable by the next agent. See the new reference doc `references/GHL-INBOUND-AND-PLAYBOOKS.md` ("JSON structure rule").

## 🗺️ EXECUTION ORDER MAP

The full playbook is sequenced into seven phases. Each phase has specific steps and ends with a mini-QC checkpoint. The final phase is the full QC + hand-off.

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ PHASE 0 — Orient                                                 │
│   O.1  Apply Teach Yourself Protocol                             │
│   O.2  Save playbook to master files folder                      │
│   O.3  Verify OpenClaw version + schema + model freshness        │

│   O.5  Locate secrets env file                                   │
│   O.6  Verify Dreaming + Embeddings config (v5.3)                │
│   O.7  Seed design principles into MEMORY.md (v5.4)              │
│   Initialize Run Manifest                                        │
│   Pre-flight checklist                                           │
│   ✅ Checkpoint A — Orientation complete                          │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ PHASE 1 — Build network plumbing                                 │
│   Step 1  Create Cloudflare tunnel + DNS CNAME                   │
│   Step 2  Install cloudflared as persistent service + restart    │
│   ✅ Checkpoint B — Tunnel verified end-to-end                    │

│ PHASE 2 — Configure OpenClaw                                     │
│   Step 3   Configure hooks.mappings for GHL inbound              │

│ PHASE 3 — Persist credentials + deliverables                     │

│   ✅ Checkpoint D — Operator has copy-paste materials             │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
```

The agent does NOT skip ahead. Each checkpoint must pass before the next phase begins. If a checkpoint fails, the agent stops and reports.

## 🤝 SUBAGENT DELEGATION PATTERN (READ BEFORE SELF-ORIENTATION)

This playbook is long (~3,000 lines) and the work is intensive. The recommended execution pattern is a **two-agent split**: the main agent stays with the operator and acts as their UI, while a dedicated **install subagent** with a high-reasoning model executes Phases 0–6 of this playbook. The main agent does NOT execute the playbook itself; it delegates.

### When to use the subagent pattern (default: YES)

Use a subagent in nearly all cases. The exceptions are narrow:

- **Skip subagent ONLY IF** OpenClaw's `sessions_send` (or equivalent agent-to-agent dispatch) is unavailable on this install, OR if the operator explicitly requests single-agent execution.
- **In all other cases**, the main agent spawns a subagent and supervises.

### Subagent architecture

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  MAIN AGENT                                                 │
│  (stays with operator, fast/cheap model, e.g. Gemini 3.1)   │
│                                                             │
│  Responsibilities:                                          │
│   • Welcome the operator, gather initial inputs             │
│   • Spawn install subagent with this full playbook          │
│   • Relay subagent's questions to operator                  │
│   • Relay operator's answers back to subagent               │
│   • Surface progress updates to operator every few steps    │
│   • Receive final summary from subagent and display         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                            ▲
                            │ progress + questions + answers
                            ▼
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  INSTALL SUBAGENT                                           │
│  (executes the playbook, HIGH-reasoning model, fresh ctx)   │
│                                                             │
│  Responsibilities:                                          │
│   • Apply Teach Yourself Protocol to ingest this playbook   │
│   • Execute Phases 0 through 6 step by step                 │
│   • At each operator decision point, send question UP to    │
│     main agent (NOT directly to operator)                   │
│   • Maintain the Run Manifest                               │
│   • Publish progress updates after each phase checkpoint    │
│   • Send final summary up to main agent at QC pass          │
│                                                             │
│  Time budget: 45 minutes (with extension allowed)           │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### Subagent model selection

The install subagent does NOT use the conversational reply model (e.g., Gemini 3.1 Flashlight). It uses a heavy-reasoning, large-context-window model because:

- The playbook is ~3,000 lines — needs a high context window to ingest fully
- Setup involves long sequential reasoning across 11 steps + 7 phases + 7 checkpoints
- One-shot quality matters more than per-token latency
- Failure cost is high (broken setup is hours of debugging)

**Recommended install subagent models (in priority order):**

1. **`deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro`** via OpenRouter or Ollama Cloud, with thinking set to `max`. ~1M context, deep reasoning, best long-instruction following.
2. **`google/gemini-3.5-flash`** via OpenRouter. ~2M context, very fast, good reasoning. Best if budget is a concern.
3. **`ollama/deepseek-v4-flash`** with `thinking: max`. Free if Ollama Cloud is configured. Slightly less capable than Pro but workable.
4. **`anthropic/claude-opus-4-7`** via Anthropic API. Highest quality if available; most expensive.

Verify model availability against `openrouter.ai/models` and `ollama.com/library` at run-time (per Self-Orientation O.3) — newer models may have superseded these.

### Question-routing protocol

When the install subagent needs an operator decision (routing agent, model preferences, knowledge sources, etc.):

1. Subagent does NOT message the operator directly.
2. Subagent uses `sessions_send` (or equivalent) to post the question UP to the main agent with a structured payload:

```json
{
  "type": "operator_question",
  "subagent_session_id": "<id>",
  "phase": "<current phase>",
  "step": "<current step>",
  "question": "<the question text the operator should see>",
  "options": ["<option 1>", "<option 2>", "..."]
}
```

3. Main agent receives this, displays it to the operator in conversational form.
4. Operator answers the main agent.
5. Main agent posts the answer DOWN to the subagent with:

```json
{
  "type": "operator_answer",
  "subagent_session_id": "<id>",
  "answer": "<the operator's answer>"
}
```

6. Subagent continues execution.

### Progress update protocol

After each phase checkpoint passes (A through G), the subagent posts a brief progress update UP to the main agent:

```json
{
  "type": "progress_update",
  "subagent_session_id": "<id>",
  "phase_completed": "Phase 2",
  "checkpoint": "C — OpenClaw responds to inbound webhooks",
  "elapsed_minutes": 18,
  "summary": "Tunnel built, OpenClaw configured, end-to-end test passed. Moving to credentials persistence."
}
```

Main agent displays a concise version to the operator: "✓ Phase 2 complete (18 min) — OpenClaw is now receiving webhooks. Moving to next phase."

### Time budget

- **Soft target:** 45 minutes for Phases 0–6
- **Hard limit:** 90 minutes — at that point the subagent must report what's incomplete and either request an extension or hand control back to the main agent
- **Per-phase soft targets** (subagent self-monitors):
  - Phase 0 (Orient): 3-5 minutes
  - Phase 1 (Network plumbing): 8-12 minutes
  - Phase 2 (OpenClaw config): 8-12 minutes
  - Phase 3 (Credentials + deliverables): 3-5 minutes
  - Phase 4 (Agent behavior): 5-8 minutes
  - Phase 5 (Advanced features): 6-10 minutes
  - Phase 6 (Capabilities playbook): 3-5 minutes

If a phase runs >2x its soft target, subagent reports a slowdown and surfaces what's taking time.

### Failure escalation

If the install subagent encounters a hard failure (per Rules of Engagement Rule 4):

1. Subagent restores backups taken so far
2. Subagent posts a failure report UP to main agent with: phase, step, error, what was restored, what's still in a partial state
3. Main agent displays this to operator and asks: "Should I retry the failing step, roll back the entire setup, or get me a human?"
4. Operator's answer flows back down. Subagent acts accordingly.

### Spawning the subagent (main agent's only Phase 0 task)

When the main agent receives this playbook from the operator, it does NOT begin execution. Instead, it walks through this exact sequence:

**Step 1 — Greet operator, confirm intent**

```
"Hi! I see you want to install or upgrade the Convert and Flow AI
system. I'll walk you through it. Before we start, a quick question
about HOW you want me to handle this."
```

**Step 2 — Ask: subagent or main agent? (EXPLICIT CHOICE)**

```
"This installation is a multi-step process (about 45 minutes). You
have two options for how I run it:

  1. RECOMMENDED — Spawn a high-reasoning subagent to handle the
     installation. I'll stay here with you as the UI: routing
     questions to you, showing you progress every 10 minutes, and
     handing back the final summary. The subagent gets a fresh
     context with a heavy model so it can think deeply through
     each step.

  2. I'll handle it myself in our current conversation. Simpler, but
     it consumes our context window — you may need to clear it
     first.

Which do you prefer? (I recommend option 1.)"
```

Wait for operator answer. Capture as `EXECUTION_MODE` = `subagent` or `main-agent`.

**Step 3 — Context window capability check (BOTH paths)**

The main agent inspects the current conversation context and decides whether the model has room to complete the installation.

```python
# Pseudocode for the main agent's reasoning:
playbook_token_estimate = 120_000  # ~4,800+ lines markdown as of v5.4 — this number grows with each version; agent should check current line count and re-estimate
current_context_used = <main agent estimates from session>
context_window_max = <known per model: gemini-3.1-flashlight=1M, gemini-3.5-flash=2M, etc.>
headroom_needed = playbook_token_estimate + 50_000  # buffer for execution

if EXECUTION_MODE == "main-agent":
    if (context_window_max - current_context_used) < headroom_needed:
        # Not enough room
        recommend_new_session = True
```

If `EXECUTION_MODE = main-agent` AND context is too tight, the main agent says:

```
"Before we start: I've checked my current context window and there
isn't enough room to safely run the full installation in this
conversation. I'd like you to run /new to start a fresh session,
then paste the playbook back to me there. /new is safer than
/compact because /compact can compress the playbook's instructions
and cause execution errors.

After you run /new and paste the playbook back, I'll pick up where
we left off."
```

If `EXECUTION_MODE = subagent`, this check still happens BUT the recommendation is different: "I have enough room to manage the subagent. The subagent will get its own fresh context, so /new isn't needed."

**Step 4 — Verify subagent model availability (subagent path only)**

```
"I'll spawn the install subagent. My default recommendation is
deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro with thinking set to 'max' (deep reasoning,
large context). Alternatives:
   - gemini-3.5-flash via OpenRouter (faster, slightly less deep)
   - ollama/deepseek-v4-flash with thinking:max (free if Ollama
     Cloud is configured)
   - claude-opus-4-7 via Anthropic API (highest quality, highest cost)

Stick with the default, or pick another?"
```

Verify the chosen model exists in the OpenClaw config and has an API key available. If not, prompt for the missing credential before spawning.

**Step 5 — Spawn the subagent (subagent path) OR begin executing (main-agent path)**

If subagent: spawn via `sessions_send` with a fresh session passing the full playbook, the system prompt, the chosen model, and the heartbeat configuration (see below).

If main-agent: begin with Self-Orientation Step O.1.

**Step 6 — Begin the relay loop (subagent path)**

Main agent now listens for two streams:
- **From subagent:** questions, progress updates, heartbeats, completion, failure
- **From operator:** answers, redirects, abort signals

Main agent routes between them.

**Step 7 — On subagent completion: display final summary, end**

When subagent posts the sealed Run Manifest, the main agent displays the final summary (Part 4 of this playbook) to the operator and ends the relay loop.

### 10-minute heartbeat protocol (subagent path)

The subagent must report progress every 10 minutes regardless of phase boundaries. This prevents the operator from sitting in silence during long phases.

**Heartbeat structure:**

```json
{
  "type": "heartbeat",
  "subagent_session_id": "<id>",
  "elapsed_minutes": <minutes since spawn>,
  "current_phase": "<Phase N: name>",
  "current_step": "<Step N.N: name>",
  "step_progress_summary": "<one sentence — what's happening right now>",
  "expected_next_milestone": "<one sentence — what's next>"
}
```

**Main agent action on heartbeat:**

Display to operator in conversational form: "Still working — at [elapsed] min, [current step], [progress summary]. Next: [next milestone]."

**Heartbeat termination (HARD CAP at 90 minutes):**

The heartbeat stops automatically when ANY of these conditions occurs:
- The subagent completes successfully (Run Manifest sealed)
- The subagent reports a hard failure
- The subagent reaches the 90-minute hard limit (per the Time Budget section above)
- The operator issues an abort signal

The heartbeat MUST NOT continue past 90 minutes. If the 90-minute hard limit is reached without completion, the main agent stops the heartbeat, asks the operator whether to grant an extension (one-time 15-minute extension allowed) or abort the run, and acts accordingly. The heartbeat does not silently persist indefinitely.

### Subagent's first action upon spawn

The install subagent, upon receiving this playbook as its initial context, begins with Self-Orientation Step O.1 (Teach Yourself Protocol). It does NOT skip the orientation phase. The subagent is a fresh context and must orient itself the same way a standalone agent would.

---

## 🧠 AGENT SELF-ORIENTATION — READ FIRST

Before doing anything else, the agent reading this playbook MUST execute these orientation steps. This is not optional.

### O.1 — Invoke the Teach Yourself Protocol on this document

Apply the Teach Yourself Protocol to this entire playbook. The Teach Yourself Protocol's job is to ingest a long instructional document, produce a concise working understanding of how to use it, and decide where the relevant fragments should land in the agent's core memory files (`MEMORY.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `TOOLS.md`). Carry only the concise working summary forward into active context. Reference the full saved document when deep detail is needed.

**CRITICAL — Bloat prevention rules for the three core .md files:**

OpenClaw's bootstrap reads `MEMORY.md`, `AGENTS.md`, and `TOOLS.md` on every agent turn. Anything written to these files becomes per-turn context cost. Bloating them slows the system measurably. The Teach Yourself Protocol MUST follow these placement rules without exception:

| File | What goes there | What does NOT go there |
|---|---|---|
| **MEMORY.md** | Durable facts that need to persist long-term and survive Dreaming consolidation (per `docs.openclaw.ai/concepts/memory` — Dreaming's Deep phase writes here). Examples: client business name, owner identity, established preferences. | Setup procedures. Playbook content. Anything that's "how-to" rather than "what is." |
| **AGENTS.md** | Behavioral instructions the agent applies on EVERY turn (classification rules, safeguards, drift checks, log-read, sentiment checks, knowledge-source consult, confidence checks). Each step kept to a SHORT block (10-30 lines max). | Long protocol explanations. Full configuration JSON. Examples. Tables. (These go in protocol docs in the master files folder — AGENTS.md just references them by file path.) |
| **TOOLS.md** | Concise tool usage instructions: when to call which skill, parameter format, output handling. One short paragraph per tool. | Tool implementation details. Long examples. Vendor documentation copies. |

**The pattern is: the full document goes to the master files folder. AGENTS.md / TOOLS.md / MEMORY.md get only the minimum essential pointers and behavioral rules.**

For every protocol or playbook this setup creates (sentiment-monitoring-protocol.md, drift-detection-protocol.md, knowledge-source-protocol.md, prompt-injection-protection-protocol.md, conversation-workflows, etc.), the rule is the same:

1. Full content → `<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/<protocol-name>.md`
2. AGENTS.md → one short Step (Step 1.2, 1.3, 1.4, etc.) with the behavioral instruction and a reference to the protocol file by path
3. MEMORY.md → nothing (unless the protocol introduces a new durable fact about the client)
4. TOOLS.md → nothing (unless the protocol requires a new tool the agent invokes — and even then, only if not already documented in OpenClaw's default tool list)

**If the agent is unsure whether content belongs in a bootstrap file or a master-files protocol doc, default to the master-files protocol doc.** AGENTS.md references can always be added; bloating AGENTS.md cannot be easily undone.

**Verify your placement decisions against `docs.openclaw.ai/concepts/memory` and `docs.openclaw.ai/concepts/dreaming`.** The OpenClaw memory system has specific semantics around which file holds durable knowledge (MEMORY.md), short-term recall (managed by memory-core), and reflection (DREAMS.md). Get the placement right or you'll fight Dreaming's consolidation logic for the rest of the client's lifecycle.

### O.2 — Locate (or, last resort, create) the client's master files folder

**This step is bulletproofed against creating duplicate folders.** Prior versions of the agent have created multiple copies of the master files folder with slightly different names (e.g., `OpenClaw Master Files`, `OpenClaw masterfiles`, `Master Files - OpenClaw`). The semantic discovery routine below MUST be followed exactly. NEVER create a new folder until ALL discovery paths have been exhausted and confirmed.

#### Step O.2.A — Semantic discovery (read-only — no writes yet)

Search these locations in this exact order:

**macOS:**
1. `~/Downloads/` (default for Mac Mini installations)
2. `~/Documents/`
3. `~/OpenClaw/`
4. `~/.openclaw/`
5. `~/Desktop/`
6. `/Applications/OpenClaw/`

**Linux / VPS:**
1. `~/openclaw/` and `~/OpenClaw/` (lowercase + capitalized)
2. `/data/` (common VPS install path)
3. `/var/openclaw/`
4. `/root/` (if running as root, which is common in VPS deployments)
5. `/home/*/` (all user home directories — check each)
6. `~/.openclaw/`
7. Any Docker volume mount paths referenced in the OpenClaw container config

**Discovery query (case-insensitive, fuzzy):**

For each location above, look for ANY directory whose name matches ANY of these patterns:

- Contains `openclaw` (case-insensitive) AND contains `master` (case-insensitive)
- Contains `claw` (case-insensitive) AND contains `master` (case-insensitive)
- Exact name `Master Files` (case-insensitive) — only matches if found inside an obviously-OpenClaw context (parent folder mentions OpenClaw, or the folder contains files like `AGENTS.md`, `MEMORY.md`, `openclaw.json`)
- Contains `openclaw` AND contains `files` (catches `OpenClaw Files`, `openclaw-master-files`, etc.)

Bash example for thorough fuzzy discovery:

```bash
# Build a list of all candidate directories with their full paths
find ~ /data /var/openclaw /root /home -maxdepth 4 -type d 2>/dev/null \
  | grep -iE '(openclaw.*master|claw.*master|openclaw.*files|master.*files)' \
  | sort -u
```

Capture ALL matches into a variable `CANDIDATE_FOLDERS`. Do not delete any of them.

#### Step O.2.B — Disambiguate if multiple matches

If `CANDIDATE_FOLDERS` has exactly one entry → use it. Set `MASTER_FILES_DIR` to that path. Skip to Step O.2.D.

If `CANDIDATE_FOLDERS` has multiple entries → DO NOT pick one automatically. Show the operator ALL candidates with their last-modified timestamps and content summaries:

```
I found multiple candidate folders that look like OpenClaw master files folders:

1. /Users/christy/Downloads/OpenClaw Master Files
   Last modified: 2026-05-15 14:32
   Contains: 47 files, 12 subfolders
   Includes: AGENTS.md, MEMORY.md, openclaw.json

2. /Users/christy/Documents/OpenClaw masterfiles
   Last modified: 2026-04-02 09:11
   Contains: 8 files
   Includes: (older partial setup — looks abandoned)

3. /Users/christy/Downloads/Claw Master Files
   Last modified: 2026-01-22 18:45
   Contains: 3 files
   Includes: (test folder from initial setup attempt)

Which one is the active master files folder?
(Reply with 1, 2, or 3 — I will NOT touch the others.)
```

Operator picks one. Set `MASTER_FILES_DIR` to that path. The unchosen folders are left alone (the agent does not delete or modify them — that's the operator's call).

#### Step O.2.C — Last resort: create a new folder

If `CANDIDATE_FOLDERS` is EMPTY after the thorough search above:

1. Ask the operator EXPLICITLY: "I couldn't find an existing master files folder. Do you want me to create one? If yes, where? (Default: `~/Downloads/OpenClaw Master Files` on Mac, `/data/openclaw-master-files` on VPS.)"

2. Wait for explicit operator confirmation. NEVER auto-create.

3. Create the folder at the confirmed path. Set `MASTER_FILES_DIR`.

#### Step O.2.D — Save the playbook + companion files

Once `MASTER_FILES_DIR` is set, copy the full playbook text into that folder as `openclaw-ghl-webhook-playbook-v5.14.md` (or whatever the current version is).

If a companion file `convert-and-flow-operator-quick-reference.md` is available in the same source location (BlackCEO Automations ships these together), save it to the master files folder too.

If a previous version of the playbook already exists in the folder (e.g., `openclaw-ghl-webhook-playbook-v5.4.md`), KEEP IT (don't delete) — the new version is added alongside as historical record. The agent only reads the latest version going forward.

#### Step O.2.E — Append to Run Manifest

```markdown
## O.2 — Master files folder discovery

- Candidates found: <N>
- Candidate paths: <list>
- Selected MASTER_FILES_DIR: <path>
- Selection reason: <single match | operator chose | newly created with operator approval>
- Previous playbook versions in folder: <list, if any>
- New playbook saved as: <full path>
```

#### Important note for the agent

**Never** create a new master files folder just because the discovery routine "didn't find one quickly." Run the FULL search. Check ALL the directories listed. If still nothing, ASK before creating. Duplicate folders cause cascading confusion across future setup runs — the agent on a later session won't know which is canonical and may bloat one folder while the other contains the real config.



### O.3 — Detect the OpenClaw version and verify the schema is current

Before editing ANY config, run:

```bash
openclaw --version
```

Then web-research `https://docs.openclaw.ai` and the OpenClaw GitHub repo (`github.com/openclaw/openclaw`) — specifically the file `docs/gateway/configuration-reference.md` on the `main` branch — to verify:

1. The `hooks.mappings` schema fields used in this playbook still exist in the current version. The top-level `hooks` keys: `enabled`, `token`, `path`, `maxBodyBytes`, `defaultSessionKey`, `allowRequestSessionKey`, `allowedSessionKeyPrefixes`, `allowedAgentIds`. The valid per-mapping (`.strict()` schema, verified on 2026.5.27) keys: `id`, `match`, `action`, `agentId`, `model`, `wakeMode`, `name`, `sessionKey`, `messageTemplate`, `textTemplate`, `deliver`, `allowUnsafeExternalContent`, `channel`, `to`, `thinking`, `timeoutSeconds`, `transform`. **NOTE: `mappings[].fallbacks` is NOT a valid key — the schema is `.strict()` and rejects it; fallback chains belong only on a model-routing config, never on a hook mapping.**
2. No new required fields have been added
3. The endpoint pattern `POST /hooks/<name>` for mapped hooks is still the way to receive nested external payloads
4. The `{{path.to.field}}` template syntax for reading payload fields still works the same way

**ALSO verify the model recommendations are still current.** The model wizard in Step 3.5 hard-codes specific model names (e.g., `google/gemini-3.1-flashlight`, `deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash`, `openrouter/free`). Models get deprecated and replaced. Before presenting the wizard to the operator, web-research:

- `https://openrouter.ai/models` — confirm the recommended fast model is still listed AND check whether a newer Flashlight-class model has been released (e.g., 3.2, 4.0). If a newer version exists at the same price/speed tier, use it instead.
- `https://ollama.com/library` — confirm DeepSeek V4 Flash is still current; check for newer DeepSeek variants at the same speed tier.
- Best-in-class signal: look for "fast", "flash", "lite", "mini", or "turbo" tagged models in the under-$1-per-million-tokens range. If a clearly-better option is available, swap it into the recommendation list and tell the operator what changed and why.

If the agent finds the schema has drifted — fields renamed, new requirements added, deprecations — OR the recommended models have been superseded, the agent has permission to adapt the playbook's instructions to current reality. Document what was changed and why, and tell the operator in the final output. Do not silently follow stale instructions.

### O.4 — Execute the Backup Protocol before any config edit

The Backup Protocol exists in the client's OpenClaw setup. Invoke it on `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` before any edits. The protocol creates a timestamped backup of the config file and logs the backup path. If the protocol is not available (older OpenClaw installs may not have it), fall back to:

```bash
cp ~/.openclaw/openclaw.json ~/.openclaw/openclaw.json.bak.$(date +%s)
```

Either way, capture the backup file path — you'll need to include it in the final output document. Do not proceed with config edits until the backup is confirmed.

### O.5 — Locate the secrets/env file

The client has a `.env`-style file where secrets are stored. Find it by searching the home directory and `~/.openclaw/` for any file matching:

- `secrets.env`, `.env`, `.openclaw.env`, `openclaw.env`
- Any file ending in `.env` whose name contains "secret", "openclaw", "claw", or "credentials"

If multiple candidates exist, ask the operator which is the canonical one. If none exists, create `~/.openclaw/secrets.env` and tell the operator that's where credentials will be stored.

The agent will APPEND credentials to this file (not overwrite). Use comment markers with timestamps to identify what was added by this playbook run.

### O.6 — Verify Dreaming + Embeddings configuration

OpenClaw has two memory-related features that materially affect how the AI behaves over time. Both are opt-in. For Convert and Flow deployments, BOTH should be turned on. The agent verifies and enables them during orientation.

**A. Embeddings provider check**

Without an embeddings provider, OpenClaw's `memory_search` falls back to keyword-only matching (per `docs.openclaw.ai/concepts/memory`). Knowledge Sources (Step 9.14) work less well. Conversation history retrieval misses semantic matches.

Check current config:

```bash
openclaw config get memory.embeddings
```

If the result is `undefined`, `null`, or contains no provider, the agent recommends enabling Google Gemini text-embedding-004 (free tier) as the default:

```bash
# Verify GEMINI_API_KEY exists in env file
grep -i 'GEMINI_API_KEY\|GOOGLE_API_KEY' "$SECRETS_ENV_FILE"
```

If no key is present, ask the operator to create one at `https://aistudio.google.com/apikey` (free tier, generous limits — 1500 requests per minute for embeddings as of May 2026), then append to env file:

```bash
echo 'GEMINI_API_KEY=<key>' >> "$SECRETS_ENV_FILE"
```

Then write the embeddings config:

```bash
openclaw config set memory.embeddings '{
  "provider": "google",
  "model": "text-embedding-004",
  "apiKeyEnv": "GEMINI_API_KEY"
}' --strict-json --merge
```

If a provider is already configured (OpenAI, Voyage, local), don't change it — log to Run Manifest and continue.

**Free tier note for the operator:** Google's free tier for text-embedding-004 covers most Convert and Flow clients comfortably. If a client crosses the rate limit (very rare for one-business deployments), they can switch to OpenAI text-embedding-3-small later by re-running this step.

**B. Dreaming enablement check**

Dreaming is OpenClaw's three-phase background memory consolidation system (Light → REM → Deep) that runs nightly and promotes high-value short-term signals into durable `MEMORY.md` entries (per `docs.openclaw.ai/concepts/dreaming`). Without it, either (a) `MEMORY.md` bloats with low-value entries, or (b) important patterns are never persisted. For long-term client deployments, Dreaming is strongly recommended.

Check current config:

```bash
openclaw config get memory.dreaming.enabled
```

If `false` or `undefined`, enable Dreaming with the standard threshold gates (per OpenClaw documentation, the default gates are conservative: minScore 0.8, minRecallCount 3, minUniqueQueries 3):

```bash
openclaw config set memory.dreaming '{
  "enabled": true,
  "schedule": "0 3 * * *",
  "phases": ["light", "rem", "deep"],
  "thresholds": {
    "minScore": 0.8,
    "minRecallCount": 3,
    "minUniqueQueries": 3
  }
}' --strict-json --merge
```

Verify the cron job appears:

```bash
openclaw cron list | grep -i dreaming
```

**Heads up to the operator:** Dreaming writes a human-readable diary at `DREAMS.md` so they can review what got consolidated. First Deep phase sweeps may take several days of activity before promoting anything — the threshold gates require repeated relevance, not single instances. This is by design (prevents promoting noise).

**C. Append to Run Manifest:**

```markdown
## O.6 — Dreaming + Embeddings configuration

- Embeddings provider: <google text-embedding-004 (free) | existing provider preserved | unable to configure>
- Dreaming enabled: <true | false>
- Dreaming schedule: <cron expression>
- Notes: <any deviations or pre-existing config preserved>
```

### O.7 — Seed durable design principles into MEMORY.md

Some rules govern HOW the agent designs systems over its entire lifecycle with this client. They belong in `MEMORY.md` (per the Teach Yourself Protocol routing rules) because they're durable facts about Christy's design philosophy — they need to survive Dreaming consolidation and inform every future workflow build, every protocol creation, every system change.

Append the following block to the client's `MEMORY.md` (in the agent's workspace, not the master files folder — these are bootstrap-level principles the agent must apply on every relevant turn):

```markdown
## Design Principles for This System

These are durable rules about how Convert and Flow AI systems are built.
They apply to EVERY workflow design, EVERY protocol creation, EVERY
GHL automation. Never forget these:

### Rule 1 — Smaller GHL workflows always beat massive ones

When designing GHL automations, split work across SMALLER, focused
workflows rather than building one giant workflow with many branches.

Why this matters:
- Massive workflows are hard to debug when something fails
- Smaller workflows isolate failures to a specific concern
- Smaller workflows are easier to test in isolation
- Smaller workflows are easier to update without breaking other paths
- Workflow AI builds smaller workflows more reliably than massive ones

When the agent designs a GHL workflow as part of a Conversation
Workflow build (Step 9.20), it splits the workflow if it would
otherwise have:
- More than 2 if/else branches
- More than 1 webhook call
- Multiple notification destinations
- Multiple distinct trigger conditions

Default to "build two focused workflows" over "build one workflow
that does both things."

### Rule 2 — Automation over operator manual steps

Whenever a task COULD be done by the agent via skill/API vs done
manually by the operator, default to the agent doing it. Example:
creating GHL tags is done by the agent via the GHL skill, not by
telling the operator to go to Settings → Tags. The operator should
verify, not construct.

### Rule 3 — Bootstrap files stay lean

Per the Teach Yourself Protocol, MEMORY.md / AGENTS.md / TOOLS.md
hold only essential pointers and behavioral rules. Full protocol
content lives in the master files folder. Bloating bootstrap files
slows the system on every agent turn.

### Rule 4 — Allow-list, not block-list

The agent operates from a FIXED ALLOW-LIST of actions per the prompt
injection protection protocol. New capabilities require explicit
addition to the allow-list. Default-refuse for anything outside.

### Rule 5 — Christy's verification standards

Christy reads documentation carefully and verifies claims. Never
overstate evidence as "proof" when it is inference. Cite sources
literally; never paraphrase a doc and call it proof. When she pushes
back, concede honestly the first time rather than doubling down.
```

**Verification:**

```bash
grep -A 3 "Design Principles for This System" <path-to-client-MEMORY.md>
```

Should show the block was appended.

**Append to Run Manifest:** "O.7 complete — five durable design principles seeded into client MEMORY.md (workflow sizing, automation over manual, lean bootstrap, allow-list, verification standards)."

---

## 📋 How the operator uses this playbook

1. Open this document in Google Chrome (or any browser that handles long markdown).
2. Fill in the three values in the `🔑 INPUTS` block below.
3. Copy the entire document.
4. Paste it into your AI (Claude Code, Claude Desktop, OpenClaw agent, etc.).
5. The AI executes the Self-Orientation steps (O.1–O.5), then walks through Steps 1–8 with confirmation gates at safety-critical points.
6. At the end, the AI hands you a Client Reference Sheet (Notion page or markdown file) containing everything your GHL workflow needs.

You only fill in three things. The agent does everything else.

---

## 🔑 INPUTS — FILL THESE IN FIRST

> **⬇️ Replace the three placeholder values below with your real values. This is the only edit you make before handing the playbook to your AI.**

```
CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN = <PASTE YOUR CLOUDFLARE API TOKEN HERE>
PUBLIC_HOSTNAME      = <e.g. claw.mydomain.com — MUST BE A SUBDOMAIN>
HOOK_NAME            = <short label, e.g. ghl-inbound>
```

### Where each value comes from

**`CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`** — Create at https://dash.cloudflare.com/profile/api-tokens using the scopes in your onboarding doc. Authorizes the AI to create the tunnel and DNS record. Never share or reuse across Cloudflare accounts.

> **🛑 NO CLOUDFLARE API TOKEN YET? — AGENT, OFFER TWO PATHS (do NOT just `cat` a guide).**
> The full step-by-step (Cloudflare account → GoDaddy nameservers → 9-permission token, ~30 min) lives in
> `references/cloudflare-godaddy-setup-guide.md`. When the client has **no Cloudflare API token**, the agent
> PROACTIVELY offers a choice of two paths and acts on whichever the client picks:
>
> - **(a) Notion doc** — create a NEW Notion doc **IN THE CLIENT'S OWN Notion workspace** (never another
>   client's, never a shared/operator workspace) containing the full content of
>   `references/cloudflare-godaddy-setup-guide.md`, then **send the client the link** so they can follow it
>   at their own pace; OR
> - **(b) Manual walkthrough** — walk the client through the guide live, step by step, answering questions.
>
> Ask which they prefer, then do it. Do NOT just emit a `cat` command — proactively offer the Notion doc +
> link or the manual walkthrough. (Per onboarding policy: every client gets their OWN Notion workspace; never
> co-mingle clients.) This mirrors the prereq-halt handling in `scripts/00-verify-prerequisites.sh`.

**`PUBLIC_HOSTNAME`** — ⚠️ **MUST be a subdomain** of a domain already in your Cloudflare account. The agent creates a fresh CNAME at this hostname.

- ✅ Works: `claw.mydomain.com`, `openclaw.mydomain.com`, `agent.mydomain.com`
- ❌ Doesn't work: `mydomain.com` (root), `www.mydomain.com` (typically already in use)

**`HOOK_NAME`** — Any short label for this mapping. `ghl-inbound` is the default. This becomes both the OpenClaw mapping id AND the URL path GHL POSTs to (`https://<host>/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>`).

# Part 1 — The Agent's Execution Playbook

## Pre-flight checklist (the agent must verify all items before proceeding)

The agent confirms each of these before touching anything. Report results to the operator.

- [ ] OS detected (macOS or Linux): `uname -a`
- [ ] Package manager available: `which brew` (macOS) or `which apt || which yum || which dnf` (Linux)
- [ ] OpenClaw installed and version captured: `openclaw --version` — version saved as `OPENCLAW_VERSION`
- [ ] OpenClaw Gateway is running: `openclaw status` (start with `openclaw gateway start` if needed)
- [ ] Gateway port detected (do NOT assume 18789):

  ```bash
  # Try these in order:
  openclaw status                                                            # a. authoritative
  cat ~/.openclaw/openclaw.json | grep -iE 'port|listen|gateway'             # b. config
  lsof -iTCP -sTCP:LISTEN -P -n | grep -i openclaw | grep 127.0.0.1          # c. process (macOS)
  ss -tlnp | grep openclaw                                                   # c. process (Linux)
  curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" http://127.0.0.1:18789/             # d. probe default
  ```
  Save as `GATEWAY_PORT`.

- [ ] Self-Orientation O.3 done: `docs.openclaw.ai` and the OpenClaw GitHub `configuration-reference.md` have been checked against `OPENCLAW_VERSION` and the `hooks.mappings` schema in this playbook still matches
- [ ] Master files folder located (per O.2) — path saved as `MASTER_FILES_DIR`
- [ ] Secrets env file located (per O.5) — path saved as `SECRETS_ENV_FILE`
- [ ] Backup Protocol fired against `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` (per O.4) — backup path saved as `CONFIG_BACKUP_PATH`

If any item fails, STOP and report to operator before proceeding.

### Initialize the Run Manifest

The Run Manifest is a markdown file the agent maintains throughout the setup, recording every step's status, every captured value, every deviation, every checkpoint result. It's the audit trail per client setup.

Create:

```bash
RUN_MANIFEST_PATH="$MASTER_FILES_DIR/run-manifest-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S).md"
```

Initialize the file with this header:

```markdown
# Run Manifest — Convert and Flow Setup

**Started:** <ISO timestamp>
**Operator:** <operator name or "unspecified">
**Client:** <client name or "unspecified">
**Playbook version:** 5.0
**OpenClaw version detected:** <OPENCLAW_VERSION>

## Captured values

(Populated as the run proceeds.)

## Phase progress

- [ ] Phase 0 — Orient
- [ ] Phase 1 — Build network plumbing
- [ ] Phase 2 — Configure OpenClaw
- [ ] Phase 3 — Persist credentials + deliverables
- [ ] Phase 4 — Install agent behavior
- [ ] Phase 5 — Install advanced features
- [ ] Phase 6 — Document agent capabilities
- [ ] Phase 7 — Full QC + hand-off

## Checkpoint results

(Each checkpoint result appended here as the agent completes phases.)

## Deviations

(Each deviation appended here per Rule 3.)

## Step log

(Each step's start time, completion status, and key outputs appended here.)
```

After every captured value (TUNNEL_ID, HOOKS_TOKEN, etc.) and every step, append to the manifest. Future agents reading this file can reconstruct exactly what happened.

### ✅ Checkpoint A — Orientation complete

Before proceeding to Phase 1, verify ALL of the following pass:

- [ ] Teach Yourself Protocol applied — concise summary in active context
- [ ] Full playbook saved to `MASTER_FILES_DIR`
- [ ] OpenClaw version detected and schema verified against live docs (Step O.3)
- [ ] Backup Protocol fired (or fallback `cp` backup taken) on `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json`
- [ ] `SECRETS_ENV_FILE` located or created
- [ ] Embeddings provider configured (Google text-embedding-004 default, per O.6) and API key present in env
- [ ] Dreaming enabled with cron `0 3 * * *` and standard threshold gates (per O.6)
- [ ] Design principles block appended to client's `MEMORY.md` (per O.7)
- [ ] Pre-flight checklist all items passed
- [ ] Run Manifest initialized at `RUN_MANIFEST_PATH`

Append checkpoint result to Run Manifest:

```markdown
## Checkpoint A — Orientation complete

**Result:** PASSED (or FAILED with reason)
**Timestamp:** <ISO>
**Notes:** <any caveats>
```

If FAILED → STOP, do not proceed to Phase 1, report to operator.
