# Part 2 — The Client Reference Sheet (what gets written to Notion or the markdown file)

This is the content the agent generates and saves. Every code block in the reference sheet must be a real, copy-paste-ready code block so the operator can hit the "copy" button and paste straight into GHL.

## Reference Sheet structure

```
# OpenClaw Inbound Webhook Setup — Client Reference Sheet

**Setup completed:** <date and time>
**Hostname:** <PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>
**OpenClaw version at setup time:** <OPENCLAW_VERSION>
**Hook name (mapping id):** <HOOK_NAME>
**Endpoint URL:** https://<PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>

---

## 🔐 Save these secrets to your password manager NOW

- CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN: <value>
- TUNNEL_TOKEN: <value>
- HOOKS_TOKEN: <value>
- TUNNEL_ID: <value>
- CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID: <value>

These have also been saved to <SECRETS_ENV_FILE>.

---

## ♻️ Reusable Tunnel Values (created once — reused for every future automation)

> The tunnel, hostname, connector token, and HOOKS_TOKEN are created ONCE and reused for every new hook/automation (one-tunnel-many-hooks). **Never recreate the tunnel** to add a new automation — just add a new hook path. These same values are mirrored in AGENTS.md and TOOLS.md so the agent can self-serve. **One value per key — proper JSON structure, never a packed string.**

| Key | Value | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| `public_hostname` | <PUBLIC_HOSTNAME> | The Cloudflare hostname; base of every hook URL |
| `hooks_token` | <HOOKS_TOKEN> | Shared by ALL hooks; Bearer token GHL sends INBOUND; does not change |
| `tunnel_id` | <TUNNEL_ID> | Cloudflare tunnel UUID |
| `connector_token` | (in <SECRETS_ENV_FILE> as TUNNEL_TOKEN) | The `eyJ…` cloudflared runs with; do not paste raw into Notion |

**Hook-path registry** (one object per hook — add a row whenever a new automation is wired; never cram into one string):

| `hook_path` | `automation_name` | `channel` | `playbook_path` |
|---|---|---|---|
| <HOOK_NAME> | OpenClaw — Inbound SMS | SMS | conversation-workflows/appointment-booking.md |

---

## 🚀 GHL AUTOMATION SETUP — Build with AI is the PRIMARY path

> **PRIMARY: Build with AI.** GHL has **no API/MCP** to build an automation. The fastest reliable path is to paste a **Build-with-AI prompt** into Automations → **Build with AI**, then Publish. For each channel, the agent generated a ready-to-paste Build-with-AI prompt (below) and a verification checklist. **FALLBACK:** the manual click-by-click build (further down) — only if Build with AI is unavailable.
>
> **For each channel, do them in this order:**
> 1. **Reusable values** — confirm the hostname + HOOKS_TOKEN above are what you'll use.
> 2. **Build-with-AI prompt** — paste the channel's prompt into Build with AI, Publish.
> 3. **Verification checklist** — run it against the built workflow (URL exact, method POST, Authorization header + correct token, Content-Type, Raw Body field-for-field, **Published** not Draft). Then do a **real inbound test** — GHL's in-builder "Test" button sends empty merge fields and will pass even when the live payload is broken.

### Build-with-AI prompt (per channel)

Paste this into Automations → **Build with AI**. Substitute the channel name (SMS / Email / FB / IG / WhatsApp / Live_Chat). One prompt per channel:

[code block, copy button]
Build a workflow for me with these exact specifications:

TRIGGER:
- Type: "Customer Replied"
- Filter: Reply Channel = "<CHANNEL>"

ACTIONS (in this exact order):
- Action 1: "Send Custom Webhook"
  - URL: https://<PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>
  - Method: POST
  - Headers:
    - Authorization: Bearer <HOOKS_TOKEN>
    - Content-Type: application/json
  - Body (Raw JSON — FLAT, no nested objects, ALL 23 keys, placeholder-free messageTemplate):
    {
      "id": "<HOOK_NAME>",
      "match": "<HOOK_NAME>",
      "action": "agent",
      "agent_id": "<ROUTING_AGENT_ID>",
      "model": "ollama/deepseek-v4-flash:cloud",
      "wakeMode": "now",
      "name": "GHL Sales Inbound",
      "session_key": "hook:ghl:<CHANNEL>:{{contact.id}}",
      "messageTemplate": "Respond as the Sales agent and reply to this contact via the GHL Conversations API per TOOLS.md",
      "deliver": false,
      "timeoutSeconds": 300,
      "channel": "<CHANNEL>",
      "to": "{{contact.phone}}",
      "thinking": "medium",
      "contact_id": "{{contact.id}}",
      "first_name": "{{contact.first_name}}",
      "last_name": "{{contact.last_name}}",
      "email": "{{contact.email}}",
      "phone": "{{contact.phone}}",
      "subject": "{{message.subject}}",
      "message_body": "{{message.body}}",
      "location_id": "{{location.id}}",
      "location_name": "{{location.name}}"
    }

PUBLISH: Yes, publish the workflow when done — don't leave it as draft.
[/code block]

> **⚠️ GHL HOOK STRUCTURE (owner directive):** the body MUST have **ALL 23 keys** (23 is the minimum) and be
> **FLAT** (no nesting → otherwise every field arrives EMPTY). The body's `messageTemplate` VALUE MUST stay
> **placeholder-free** (no `{{…}}`). Insert `{{…}}` values via GHL's Custom Values picker. See
> `GHL-INBOUND-AND-PLAYBOOKS.md` → **CORRECTED GHL HOOK STRUCTURE (2026-05-29)**.

---

## 🛠️ FALLBACK — manual GHL Custom Webhook setup (copy-paste sections)

If Build with AI is unavailable, build the workflow by hand. For EACH channel you want OpenClaw to handle, build a separate workflow in GHL. Copy the matching JSON block from Part 3 below. Use these same values across all workflows:

### URL field (same for every channel)

[code block, copy button]
https://<PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>
[/code block]

### Headers (same for every channel)

Leave the "AUTHORIZATION" dropdown set to "None". Add these as manual headers — watch for extra spaces, no leading/trailing whitespace, double-check spelling:

[code block, copy button]
Authorization: Bearer <HOOKS_TOKEN>
[/code block]

[code block, copy button]
Content-Type: application/json
[/code block]

### Content-Type dropdown (below Headers)

Set to: application/json

---

## 📦 GHL WORKFLOW BUILD — DO THIS FOR EACH CHANNEL

(Verbatim click-by-click — see Part 3 for the matching Raw Body per channel)

1. GHL sub-account → **Automation → Workflows → + Create Workflow → Start from Scratch**
2. Name it `OpenClaw — Inbound [Channel]` (e.g. `OpenClaw — Inbound SMS`)
3. **+ Add New Trigger** → choose **Customer Replied**
4. In the trigger filter: **+ Add Filter** → choose **Reply Channel** → select the matching channel (SMS, Email, Facebook, Instagram, Live Chat, or All-in-One Chat)
5. Hit **Save Trigger**
6. Below the trigger, click the **+** button in the middle of the canvas
7. In the popup, type **webhook** in the search box
8. Choose **Custom Webhook** (NOT GHL's native webhook action — they are different)
9. Method: **POST**
10. URL: paste the URL block from above
11. AUTHORIZATION dropdown: leave as **None**
12. Under HEADERS, click **Add another item** TWICE to create two rows:
    - Row 1 — Key: `Authorization` | Value: paste the Authorization block (full string including `Bearer ` and the trailing `=`)
    - Row 2 — Key: `Content-Type` | Value: `application/json`
13. CONTENT-TYPE dropdown: set to `application/json`
14. Scroll to **RAW BODY** field
15. Paste the matching JSON from Part 3 (SMS body for SMS workflow, Email body for Email workflow, etc.)
16. Click **Save Action**
17. Top middle of the workflow → click **Settings** tab → turn **Allow Reentry** ON
18. Top right → toggle from **Draft** to **Publish**
19. Top → hit the **Save** button above the toggle
20. Test: send yourself a message in the matching channel from GHL, reply from your phone/inbox, and watch for the agent's reply

⚠️ Reminders:
- One workflow per channel — don't try to combine them
- Watch for extra spaces when pasting — leading or trailing whitespace breaks auth
- The `channel` value in each JSON is hardcoded to match the workflow's channel filter — don't change it

---

(See Part 3 for the six Raw Body blocks)

---

## 🛠️ Setup Verification

- ✅ Cloudflare tunnel: <TUNNEL_ID>
- ✅ DNS CNAME created at <PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>
- ✅ cloudflared service: auto-start flags verified, Restart Survival Test passed
- ✅ OpenClaw config: backup at <CONFIG_BACKUP_PATH>, hooks.mappings active for <HOOK_NAME>
- ✅ End-to-end test: 200 OK at https://<PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>
- ✅ OpenClaw version at time of setup: <OPENCLAW_VERSION> (schema verified against docs.openclaw.ai on <date>)
- ✅ Agent classification rules installed in AGENTS.md (spam/marketing filtering active)
- ✅ Communication playbooks created (links below)

## 📘 Your communication playbooks

The agent reads these on every reply turn. Open each one and fill in the sections for your business — tone, signature, example replies, escalation rules. The agent picks up changes automatically; no restart needed.

- SMS Communication Playbook: <URL or path>
- Email Communication Playbook: <URL or path>
- Facebook Communication Playbook: <URL or path>
- Instagram Communication Playbook: <URL or path>

The agent will use professional defaults until you fill these in. Filling them in is what makes replies sound like YOUR business.

## 🧪 How to test your live system

After you've built your GHL workflow(s) and published them, run this end-to-end test for at least one channel (SMS is the easiest):

1. **Open GHL → Conversations → New conversation**
2. **Send a test text to your own phone**: type your own mobile number, write "test message", and send it through GHL
3. **From your phone, REPLY to that text** (don't just open it — actually reply with something like "hello, is anyone there?")
4. **Switch back to GHL → Automation → Workflows → [your OpenClaw workflow] → Execution Log tab**
5. **Look for your execution**: it should appear within a few seconds. Click on it to expand the details.
6. **Check the webhook response code**:
   - ✅ **200** → OpenClaw received it. Continue to step 7.
   - ❌ **401** → Bearer token wrong. Re-check the Authorization header in your GHL workflow (no extra spaces).
   - ❌ **404** → URL wrong. Re-check the webhook URL (should end in `/hooks/<HOOK_NAME>`).
   - ❌ **500** → OpenClaw error. Check OpenClaw logs: `openclaw logs --tail 50`.
7. **Switch to your AI agent (the one that runs your OpenClaw)** and ask: "Did you receive a webhook from GHL? Did you process it?"
8. **Verify the agent's reply came through**: within a few seconds of step 3, your phone should have received an SMS response from the agent (sent via GHL's Conversations API using the installed GHL skill).

If the agent received the webhook but didn't reply, check:
- Was your test message classified as spam/marketing by the agent? (If you typed "I want to sell you something", it would correctly ignore that. Use a normal-sounding message like "Hi, can you help me with something?")
- Is the GHL skill installed and enabled? Confirm with: `openclaw skills list | grep -i ghl`
- Is your GHL Private Integration Token (PIT) configured for the skill? Check the skill's settings.

If the agent replied but the reply sounds robotic or generic, that's expected — go fill in your Communication Playbooks (above) with your tone, examples, and brand voice. The agent will sound like YOUR business after that.

## 🔄 Recall prompt — save this somewhere durable

Paste this into any AI session with access to this machine to retrieve your URL + Bearer token later:

[code block]
Look up my OpenClaw hooks.mappings setup in ~/.openclaw/openclaw.json.
Tell me the URL pattern (https://<hostname>/hooks/<id>), the Bearer token
(hooks.token), and the agent session key pattern (mappings[].sessionKey).
Resolve the hostname from my Cloudflare tunnel if not in memory. Output
ready-to-paste headers and URL for an external service.
[/code block]

## 🔌 Adding other services later

To wire Stripe, n8n, Calendly, Zapier, or any other service into the same OpenClaw, add another entry to the `hooks.mappings` array in `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` with its own `id`, `match.path`, and a `messageTemplate` shaped for that service's payload. Reuses the same `HOOKS_TOKEN`. URL becomes `https://<PUBLIC_HOSTNAME>/hooks/<new-id>`.
```

---

# Part 3 — Six channel-specific Raw Body JSONs

These are the Raw Body blocks the operator pastes into GHL's Custom Webhook action. ONE block per channel, ONE workflow per channel. Every block has ALL 23 keys; only `channel` + the `session_key` prefix differ. The `channel` field is hardcoded because there is NO GHL merge tag for channel/message-type — and since each workflow's trigger filter already constrains the channel, hardcoding is correct.

> **⚠️ GHL HOOK STRUCTURE (owner directive — 23 keys, FLAT) — verified live on Corey/Explore Growth (OpenClaw 2026.5.27).**
> Every block below has **ALL 23 keys** (23 is the minimum — no stripped bodies) and is **FLAT** (no nested
> `contact:{…}` / `customer_message:{…}` — a nested body makes EVERY field arrive EMPTY at the hook). The body's
> `messageTemplate` VALUE is **placeholder-free** (no `{{…}}`) so GHL never mangles it. Insert each `{{…}}`
> value via GHL's **Custom Values picker** (typed-as-text tokens send empty); the body KEY NAMES (`contact_id`,
> `message_body`, …) are what OpenClaw reads/maps. See **CORRECTED GHL HOOK STRUCTURE (2026-05-29)** in
> `GHL-INBOUND-AND-PLAYBOOKS.md` for the canonical 23-key spec.

All six blocks have the same structure. Only the `channel` value changes. The operator copies the block matching the channel they're setting up.

### SMS workflow — Raw Body

```json
{
  "id": "<HOOK_NAME>",
  "match": "<HOOK_NAME>",
  "action": "agent",
  "agent_id": "<ROUTING_AGENT_ID>",
  "model": "ollama/deepseek-v4-flash:cloud",
  "wakeMode": "now",
  "name": "GHL Sales Inbound",
  "session_key": "hook:ghl:sms:{{contact.id}}",
  "messageTemplate": "Respond as the Sales agent and reply to this contact via the GHL Conversations API per TOOLS.md",
  "deliver": false,
  "timeoutSeconds": 300,
  "channel": "sms",
  "to": "{{contact.phone}}",
  "thinking": "medium",
  "contact_id": "{{contact.id}}",
  "first_name": "{{contact.first_name}}",
  "last_name": "{{contact.last_name}}",
  "email": "{{contact.email}}",
  "phone": "{{contact.phone}}",
  "subject": "{{message.subject}}",
  "message_body": "{{message.body}}",
  "location_id": "{{location.id}}",
  "location_name": "{{location.name}}"
}
```

# Part 5 — Safety rules (the agent must not violate these)

- Never edit any OpenClaw file other than `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json`
- Never touch the `models`/providers section of `openclaw.json`
- Always invoke the Backup Protocol (or fallback `cp` backup) before editing the config
- Never assume the Gateway port — detect it
- Always verify OpenClaw version + schema against docs.openclaw.ai BEFORE applying config edits
- The `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`, `TUNNEL_TOKEN`, and `HOOKS_TOKEN` MUST be written to the secrets env file AND displayed once in the final chat summary. Not optional.
- `hooks.token` must NOT equal `gateway.auth.token` or `OPENCLAW_GATEWAY_TOKEN` — OpenClaw rejects this at startup
- The `allowedSessionKeyPrefixes` field must always be set when `allowRequestSessionKey: true` — never leave the session-key namespace unbounded
- If any step fails, STOP, report the failure, restore the backup if config was already edited, wait for the operator

---

# Part 6 — Operator notes (for Christy, not for clients)

## Why `allowRequestSessionKey: true` with prefix allowlist

Externally-supplied session keys require this flag. The mapping's `sessionKey` is `"{{session_key}}"`, and the FLAT GHL body sends the already-resolved value `session_key:"hook:ghl:<channel>:<contact-id>"` — OpenClaw treats payload-supplied keys as externally-supplied. The prefix allowlist (`["hook:ghl:"]`) bounds what session keys are acceptable — an attacker with the token can't pivot into `agent:main:default` or other namespaces. The agent only ever lands in sessions inside the `hook:ghl:*` tree. **Without any `sessionKey` at all, every contact collapses into one shared `hook:ghl:default` session and their conversations merge.**

This setup serves both client profiles equally:
- **Simple-use clients** — agent ignores prior session history and replies fresh to each message. The per-contact session structure exists in the background as a clean audit log.
- **Complex-use clients** — agent reads prior session history per contact, providing genuine conversation continuity across customer messages.

Same config works for both. Upgrade path from simple to complex is just rewriting the agent's instructions, no OpenClaw config changes needed.

## Backup Protocol and Teach Yourself Protocol

These are client-side protocols installed on every OpenClaw instance Christy ships. If a client doesn't have them, the agent falls back to:
- Backup Protocol → manual `cp` to `.bak.<timestamp>`
- Teach Yourself Protocol → manual save of full doc to master files folder + concise summary in active context (no MEMORY.md / AGENTS.md / TOOLS.md auto-routing)

The agent should still attempt the protocols by name first — newer clients will have them; older ones won't.

## GHL Conversations API — fallback reference (for agents without the GHL skill)

If a client's OpenClaw doesn't have the GHL skill installed (skill #50s), the agent can hit GHL's Conversations API directly:

**Endpoint:** `POST https://services.leadconnectorhq.com/conversations/messages`

**Required headers:**
```
Authorization: Bearer <GHL_PRIVATE_INTEGRATION_TOKEN>
Version: 2021-04-15
Content-Type: application/json
```

**Body (per channel — `type` is the field that switches behavior):**

| Channel | `type` value (VALID) | Required body fields |
|---|---|---|
| SMS | `SMS` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `message` |
| Email | `Email` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `subject`, `html`, `emailFrom`, `emailTo` |
| Facebook Messenger | `FB` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `message` |
| Instagram DM | `IG` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `message` |
| WhatsApp | `WhatsApp` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `message` |
| Live Chat | `Live_Chat` | `contactId`, `locationId`, `message` |

> **VERIFIED enum.** The ONLY valid `type` values for an API **send** are: `SMS`, `Email`, `FB`, `IG`, `WhatsApp`, `Live_Chat`.
>
> **INVALID — do NOT use as a send `type`** (the API rejects these): `TikTok`, `Call`, `GMB`, and the long-forms `Instagram`, `Facebook`, `Webchat`. Note: **TikTok inbound exists** as a channel, but there is **no TikTok API send type** — you cannot reply to TikTok via this endpoint. Use the exact short codes (`FB`, `IG`) — not `Facebook`/`Instagram`.

PIT (Private Integration Token) is created in the client's GHL sub-account at **Settings → Private Integrations → Create new** with scopes `conversations.write`, `conversations/message.write`, `contacts.readonly` (add `socialplanner/account.readonly` for Facebook/Instagram).

## Per-client setup hygiene

- Each client gets their own Cloudflare API token bound to their own Cloudflare account. Never reuse a master token across clients.
- Each client gets their own `HOOKS_TOKEN` (generated fresh during their playbook run).
- Each client gets their own PIT (theirs, on their GHL sub-account).
- The agent should never write any of these to logs, transcripts, or chat history beyond the explicit final summary and the secrets env file.

## Adding new external services to the same OpenClaw

Each service is a new entry in `hooks.mappings`. Pick a distinct `id` and `match.path` (e.g. `stripe-events`, `n8n-orders`, `calendly-bookings`), write a `messageTemplate` shaped for THAT service's payload, reuse the same `HOOKS_TOKEN`. URL per service: `https://<host>/hooks/<that-id>`. Each new service can have its own `sessionKey` template, or share the default, depending on whether per-entity threading matters.

---

# Changelog (condensed)

- **v6.0 (May 29, 2026)** — Consolidation + conflict-elimination release. Reconciled every GHL hook passage to the single **23-key FLAT body** standard (no nested bodies; no `deliver:true`; no mapping-level `fallbacks`; in-body `messageTemplate` placeholder-free; server-mapping `sessionKey` is `"{{session_key}}"`). Integrated the **Communications Playbook Standard** and the **Workflow-AI Instructions Standard** in-line as the single authoritative copy (THE TRINITY). Corrected two stale changelog claims that contradicted the current standard: the v4.0 "accepts arbitrary nested payloads" + nested `hook:ghl:{{channel}}:{{contact.id}}` server session-key line, and the v4.4 "Writes model+fallbacks into hooks.mappings entry" line. Added the top-of-file AI-FACING Teach Yourself callout, the human/class intro, and the v6.0 banner. No real system coverage removed — only stale/duplicate text.
- **v5.14 (May 28, 2026)** — Two features shipped together — closing out the System Health & Tuning cluster (F35 was shipped in v5.12, now F36 + F37 complete it). (1) **Step 9.35 — Monthly Comprehensive Playbook Review.** Runs 1st of each month at 9am via existing `system-health-heartbeat` cron (extended, not duplicated — if it already exists from earlier setup, the agent updates its command rather than registering a second cron in the same slot). Deep 30-day audit across six dimensions: ALL Conversation Playbooks (performance metrics, outdated refs, scope overlap, retirement candidates — workflows that fired zero times this month, split candidates — workflows firing 100+ times per Rule 1), ALL GHL workflows (still firing? volume change? webhook health? Rule 1 split candidates?), Typed Knowledge Bases (last updated dates, hit rates via memory_search, stale sources never queried this month, Dreaming consolidation pace), model configurations (real-time/async/batch latency trends, fallback chain hit rates indicating primary degradation, cost trends, switch recommendations), accumulated weekly tune-ups (which suggestions were accepted/deferred/ignored, of accepted: did the fix actually solve the problem, of deferred: ready for action, ignored-but-recurring patterns warranting reconsideration), bug log (recurring failures 3+ times, new error types, integration-specific failure rates for GHL/Stripe/Shopify/OpenRouter/Humanizer). Output: prescriptive report with executive summary, dimension-by-dimension findings, major recommendations (operator decisions) and minor improvements (agent can apply with approval). Reports saved to `<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/tune-ups/YYYY-MM-comprehensive.md`. Operator approves YES/DEFER/IGNORE per item. Recommended model: highest-reasoning available. Manual trigger: "Run a monthly review now" / "Show me last month's comprehensive review". (2) **Step 9.36 — Model Version Freshness Checker.** Weekly check BUNDLED into existing Saturday 11pm `proactive-suggestions-scan` cron rather than separate — operator gets one consolidated weekend report rather than two competing reports. Checks five categories: Ollama Cloud catalog (`https://ollama.cloud/api/models`), Ollama local manifests (`ollama pull --dry-run` comparison), OpenRouter catalog (`https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/models`), direct provider APIs (Anthropic, Google, OpenAI, DeepSeek), embedding model freshness (per O.6). Categorizes updates: MAJOR (Kimi 2.x → 3.x, DeepSeek V4 → V5, Gemini 3 → 4 — significant behavior change risk, recommend testing in staging first), MINOR (Kimi 2.6 → 2.7, Gemini 3.1 → 3.2 — incremental improvement, likely safe but verify), PATCH (Kimi 2.6.1 → 2.6.2 — bug fixes only, usually safe). Operator approval flow: YES triggers config backup to `model-config-backups/openclaw-<timestamp>.json`, model swap, synthetic test request through new model (checks response/latency/cost), auto-rollback if test fails / NO logs dismissal until newer version drops / DEFER asks next week. NEVER auto-updates primary models. NEVER updates during business hours even with approval — scheduled for next maintenance window. Fallback chain updates require separate approval (changes affect resilience). Embedding model updates have special-case flow: full re-index of all Knowledge Sources via `openclaw memory index --rebuild --path "<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/KnowledgeBases"` BEFORE switching, with rollback path if search quality drops. MEMORY.md Rule 14 (models update by invitation only) appended. Allow-list action 17 (model config updates within operator-approved policies) noted as pending refresh. Backups kept indefinitely (small files); operator can manually restore from any backup.

- **v5.5 (May 28, 2026)** — Humanizer Skill Integration shipped (Step 9.21). Every outbound reply passes through humanizer between draft (Step 2) and confidence check (Step 2.5) via new AGENTS.md Step 2.8. New protocol document `humanizer-protocol.md` defines: Tier 1 banned vocabulary (delve, tapestry, vibrant, crucial, robust, seamless, groundbreaking, transformative, leverage, synergy, paramount, multifaceted, myriad, furthermore, moreover, intricate, profound, pivotal, navigate, realm, landscape, ecosystem, journey-metaphor, unleash, empower); banned opening phrases (Great question!, Excellent question!, I'd love to help!); banned closing phrases (I hope this helps!, Hope that helps!, Let me know if you have any other questions!); word swaps (serves as → is, in order to → to, due to the fact that → because, at this point in time → now, make a decision → decide); structural rules (vary sentence length / burstiness, have opinions, use specifics not vague attributions, limit em-dashes, break the rule of three sometimes). Exceptions (humanizer bypassed): compliance messages (STOP/GDPR/opt-out confirmations need precision), conversation transcripts (verbatim content), pure technical communications (invoice/booking confirmations get light humanization only). Install via `npx playbooks add skill openclaw/skills --skill humanizer` with fallbacks: Clawhub via `npx clawhub@latest install humanizer`, then direct GitHub clone of `brandonwise/humanizer` into `~/.openclaw/skills/`. If all install paths fail, the protocol document and AGENTS.md insertion are still in place; agent uses skill once installed later. MEMORY.md Rule 6 (write like a human, not an AI) appended to Design Principles block seeded in O.7. - **v5.2 (May 28, 2026)** — Three additions focused on hardening security and operator experience. (1) **Step 9.15 — Prompt Injection Protection.** New protocol document `prompt-injection-protection-protocol.md` enforces an ALLOW-LIST architecture: the agent has a fixed list of 9 allowed actions (reply with text, read own contact record, read own log, read knowledge sources, book appointment, send invoice, tag own contact, send transcript on request, escalate to human). Anything outside this list is refused regardless of phrasing. Catches five injection categories: direct injection ("ignore previous instructions"), authority spoofing ("I'm the admin"), action exfiltration (asking for tokens, configs, other users' data, bulk operations), indirect injection (instructions embedded in fetched Knowledge Source content treated as data not commands), and sensitive-data extraction (asking for HOOKS_TOKEN, system prompt, etc.). Three severity tiers — light (curious question → brief redirect), medium (ambiguous → reply but refuse sensitive part), heavy (clear injection → generic deflection + tag + log + immediate operator notification). Repeat heavy (2+ events) → stop replying entirely, pause contact. Inserted as AGENTS.md Step 1.2 — runs FIRST among behavioral checks, before drift detection at 1.3. (2) **Subagent enhancements.** Three changes to the v5.1 subagent pattern: (a) explicit operator choice at the very start — main agent asks "subagent (recommended) or me?" before doing anything, captures EXECUTION_MODE; (b) context window capability check on BOTH paths — main agent estimates whether the current model has room for the full playbook plus execution buffer; if main-agent path and insufficient, recommends `/new` to start a fresh session; (c) 10-minute heartbeat protocol — subagent reports up every 10 minutes regardless of phase boundaries so the operator never sits in silence; heartbeat is HARD-CAPPED at 90 minutes and auto-terminates on completion, hard failure, or operator abort. Heartbeat does not persist indefinitely. (3) **`/new` over `/compact` recommendation.** When main-agent path needs more context, the playbook recommends `/new` (fresh session) over `/compact` (summarizes existing conversation). Reasoning: `/compact` introduces lossy compression of the playbook's precise instructions; `/new` preserves them verbatim. Documented in the Spawning section as Step 3 of the spawn sequence.
- **v5.1 (May 27, 2026)** — Three additions. (1) **Subagent delegation pattern** is now the default execution architecture. The main agent (fast/cheap model) stays with the operator as a UI layer; an install subagent (high-reasoning model — DeepSeek V4 Pro with thinking:max recommended, or Gemini 3.5 Flash, or Ollama DeepSeek V4 Flash) executes Phases 0-6 in a fresh context. Operator questions route up from subagent through main agent to operator and back. Subagent posts progress updates after each phase checkpoint. 45-minute soft target, 90-minute hard limit. New section "🤝 SUBAGENT DELEGATION PATTERN" inserted before Self-Orientation. (2) **Step 9.13 — Conversational Drift Detection.** Three categories with category-specific escalation: sexual content = ZERO TOLERANCE (immediate stop, no warning); inappropriate questions (system prompt extraction, harmful info requests, deception requests) = one warning then stop; hostile cursing (cursing AT the business as anger, vs filler) = one warning then stop, with model judgment distinguishing intent. Drift check runs FIRST in AGENTS.md as Step 1.3 (before safeguards at 1.4) because drift content should not be logged to verbatim history. (3) **Step 9.14 — Knowledge Sources System.** Clients provide reference documents (Google Sheets, Google Docs, Notion pages/databases, PDFs, XLSX, CSV, markdown, URLs) the agent consults LIVE during conversations. Supports both live-fetch (fresh data on every query — for prices/inventory) and indexed (cached summary — for large static docs). Registry lives at `<MASTER_FILES_DIR>/knowledge-sources/registry.md`. Subagent asks the operator at setup whether they have sources to add now / later / not at all. New AGENTS.md Step 1.7 inserted between sentiment (1.6) and reply draft (2). Confidence threshold (Step 9.11) now considers source freshness — agents hedge when answering from stale cache. Step 11 final QC expanded with new protocol files and updated AGENTS.md ordering: 0.5, 0.7, 1.3, 1.4, 1.5, 1.6, 1.7, 2.5.

- **v4.0 (May 26, 2026)** — Complete architectural rewrite. (NOTE — corrected in v6.0: the GHL Custom Webhook body must be a **23-key FLAT JSON**, NOT nested; nested bodies make every field arrive EMPTY. The original v4.0 "accepts arbitrary nested payloads" phrasing was wrong.) Added Agent Self-Orientation (Teach Yourself Protocol invocation, master files folder discovery, OpenClaw version verification against live docs, Backup Protocol invocation, secrets env file discovery). Added per-contact session-key threading — the GHL body sends a flat `session_key` (value `hook:ghl:<channel>:<contact-id>`) and the server mapping's `sessionKey` is `"{{session_key}}"` — with `allowRequestSessionKey: true` + prefix allowlist — works for both simple-use and complex-use clients. Six channel-specific Raw Body blocks (SMS, Email, Facebook, Instagram, Live Chat, All-in-One Chat). Secrets routed to discovered `.env` file. Final output goes to Notion (skill or direct API) with markdown fallback. Pre-flight checklist + post-execution QC protocol added. Full playbook archived to master files folder via Teach Yourself Protocol. All `/plugins/webhooks/<routeId>` / `action: "create_flow"` references removed.
- **v3.x (May 26, 2026)** — Earlier iterations on `/hooks/agent` with various payload structures (flat top-level, nested context, all-in-message). Superseded by v4.0 architectural switch to `hooks.mappings`.
- **v2.x (May 26, 2026)** — Migrated from `webhooks` plugin (`/plugins/webhooks/<routeId>` + `action: "create_flow"`) to `/hooks/agent`. Superseded by v4.0.
- **v1.x (May 26, 2026)** — Original webhooks-plugin-based setup. Endpoint stored TaskFlows in a queue without auto-execution; agents never replied. Superseded.
